<p><b>Steven "Steve" McManaman</b> (born 11 February 1972) is a retired English <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">footballer</a> who played as a <a href="/wiki/Midfielder" title="Midfielder">midfielder</a>, <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Winger" title="Midfielder">winger</a> and <a href="/wiki/Playmaker" title="Playmaker">playmaker</a> for <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a>, <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lfcp_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-lfcp-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-3">[3]</a></sup> McManaman is the most decorated English footballer to have played for a club abroad, with the <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a> website stating that "of all England's footballing exports in the modern era, none was as successful as McManaman."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uefa_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-uefa-5">[5]</a></sup> He is a regular pundit on <a href="/wiki/BT_Sport" title="BT Sport">BT Sport</a> football coverage.</p>
<p>After nine years at Liverpool, during which time he won the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League_Cup" title="Football League Cup">League Cup</a>, McManaman moved to Real Madrid in 1999. The transfer became one of the most controversial and high-profile <a href="/wiki/Bosman_ruling" title="Bosman ruling">Bosman rulings</a> of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> He became the first English player to win the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> with a non-English club in 2000, and two years later became the first English player to win the Champions League twice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wing_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-wing-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wing_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-wing-8">[8]</a></sup> He also won <a href="/wiki/La_Liga" title="La Liga">La Liga</a> twice before moving to Manchester City in 2003, and retiring from football in 2005. After his retirement he worked as a football <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pundit_(expert)" title="Pundit (expert)">pundit</a> for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Setanta_Sports" title="Setanta Sports">Setanta Sports</a>, <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a> and <a href="/wiki/BT_Sport" title="BT Sport">BT Sport</a>. In 2008, he was ranked third in a Top 10 of the greatest British footballers to play overseas, just behind <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Keegan" title="Kevin Keegan">Kevin Keegan</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Charles" title="John Charles">John Charles</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_career">Club career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steve_McManaman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Club career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Steve_McManaman_2009.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1951" data-file-width="1219" height="272" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Steve_McManaman_2009.jpg/170px-Steve_McManaman_2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Steve_McManaman_2009.jpg/255px-Steve_McManaman_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Steve_McManaman_2009.jpg/340px-Steve_McManaman_2009.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>

McManaman at a memorial match for <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> in 2009.</div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Liverpool">Liverpool</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steve_McManaman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Liverpool">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_days">Early days</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steve_McManaman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early days">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>McManaman grew up as an <a href="/wiki/Everton_F.C." title="Everton F.C.">Everton</a> supporter,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-evertonian_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-evertonian-10">[10]</a></sup> but when Everton offered the player a one-year contract (after McManaman had made a name for himself at tournaments for school and around <a href="/wiki/Merseyside" title="Merseyside">Merseyside</a>), McManaman's father rejected it in favour of a schoolboy contract and two-year apprenticeship offer from <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-evertonian_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-evertonian-10">[10]</a></sup> McManaman signed as a 16-year-old apprentice upon leaving school in 1988.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lfcp_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-lfcp-2">[2]</a></sup> As an apprentice, McManaman was under the mentoring of <a href="/wiki/John_Barnes_(footballer)" title="John Barnes (footballer)">John Barnes</a> whom he was being groomed to replace.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-liverpoolfc.tv_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-liverpoolfc.tv-11">[11]</a></sup> A natural <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sportsperson" title="Sportsperson">athlete</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cross_country_running" title="Cross country running">cross country</a> champion at school level (once beating <a href="/wiki/Curtis_Robb" title="Curtis Robb">Curtis Robb</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-13">[13]</a></sup> he developed through the youth scheme at Liverpool and signed as a full professional on 19 February 1990 in what was to be <a href="/wiki/Kenny_Dalglish" title="Kenny Dalglish">Kenny Dalglish</a>'s final full season as manager.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lfch_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-lfch-14">[14]</a></sup> He made his Liverpool debut under Dalglish as a substitute for <a href="/wiki/Peter_Beardsley" title="Peter Beardsley">Peter Beardsley</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_First_Division" title="Football League First Division">Football League First Division</a> on 15 December 1990, in a 2â0 league win over <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_United_F.C." title="Sheffield United F.C.">Sheffield United</a> at <a href="/wiki/Anfield" title="Anfield">Anfield</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LFCHistory.net_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-LFCHistory.net-15">[15]</a></sup> and made his full debut in a 2â1 win over <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oldham_Athletic" title="Oldham Athletic">Oldham Athletic</a> the following season, when <a href="/wiki/Graeme_Souness" title="Graeme Souness">Graeme Souness</a> had become the new manager.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-liverpoolfc.tv_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-liverpoolfc.tv-11">[11]</a></sup> He scored his first ever professional goal with a diving header four days later on 21 August 1991 in the 2â1 defeat to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a> at <a href="/wiki/Maine_Road" title="Maine Road">Maine Road</a>.</p>
<p>McManaman's performances in his first season in 1991â92 established him as a regular first team player, making 51 appearances in total, a result of both his form and his being thrown in the deep end after his mentor, Barnes, suffered a career threatening <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Achilles_Tendon" title="Achilles Tendon">Achilles Tendon</a> injury.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> He created and scored several goals that year and collected a winner's medal in the <a href="/wiki/1992_FA_Cup_Final" title="1992 FA Cup Final">1992 FA Cup Final</a> as Liverpool triumphed 2â0 against <a href="/wiki/Sunderland_A.F.C." title="Sunderland A.F.C.">Sunderland</a> and was named as the <a href="/wiki/Man_of_the_match" title="Man of the match">man of the match</a> having set up the winner for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Michael_Thomas_(footballer_born_1967)" title="Michael Thomas (footballer born 1967)">Michael Thomas</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lfch_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-lfch-14">[14]</a></sup> despite being the youngest player on the pitch. He also featured heavily in their run to the quarter-finals of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup" title="UEFA Cup">UEFA Cup</a>. His performances saw McManaman described by <a href="/wiki/Ian_Rush" title="Ian Rush">Ian Rush</a> as the most promising young player at Liverpool.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lfch_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-lfch-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Success_and_fame">Success and fame</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steve_McManaman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Success and fame">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Although McManaman had a couple of quieter seasons with the advent of the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a>, he continued to develop a reputation as one of English football's two best emerging young wingers alongside <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Giggs" title="Ryan Giggs">Ryan Giggs</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manchester_United" title="Manchester United">Manchester United</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wing_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-wing-8">[8]</a></sup> with both players known to "embarrass defences with their mazy runs, which too often lack the finishing touch they deserve."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/1993%E2%80%9394_in_English_football" title="1993â94 in English football">1993â94</a>, McManaman showed fine form with two goals against <a href="/wiki/Swindon_Town_F.C." title="Swindon Town F.C.">Swindon Town</a> and some assists including a spectacular run and assist against <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a>. However this form faltered following a confidence drop after an incident with <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Grobbelaar" title="Bruce Grobbelaar">Bruce Grobbelaar</a> towards the end of a <a href="/wiki/Merseyside_derby" title="Merseyside derby">Merseyside derby</a>, when the players exchanged blows after Grobelaar lambasted McManaman for a poor clearance which led to a goal being conceded (an incident later named as one of the top five bust ups between team mates in Premier League history).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_in_English_football" title="1994â95 in English football">1994â95</a>, McManaman got a new million pound contract, and was given a central, freer role by new coach <a href="/wiki/Roy_Evans" title="Roy Evans">Roy Evans</a>, who wanted to utilise McManaman's natural running and dribbling ability to drift all over the park. It proved a successful decision as McManaman began mesmerising defences with runs that were later to become hallmarks of the Liverpool side of the 1990s. That season he collected a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League_Cup" title="Football League Cup">League Cup</a> winner's medal after scoring twice in his side's 2â1 win over <a href="/wiki/Bolton_Wanderers_F.C." title="Bolton Wanderers F.C.">Bolton</a>; such was his performance that fans named it <a href="/wiki/1995_Football_League_Cup_Final" title="1995 Football League Cup Final">"The McManaman Final"</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> For his second <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_(1923)" title="Wembley Stadium (1923)">Wembley</a> final appearance in succession he was awarded man of the match, earning the <a href="/wiki/Alan_Hardaker_Trophy" title="Alan Hardaker Trophy">Alan Hardaker Trophy</a> and a tribute from guest of honour, celebrated veteran winger <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sir_Stanley_Matthews" title="Sir Stanley Matthews">Sir Stanley Matthews</a>, who exclaimed after the final: "He reminds me of me when I was playingÂ ...<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> I wish there are more dribblers like him."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>By the end of <a href="/wiki/1995%E2%80%9396_in_English_football" title="1995â96 in English football">1995â96</a>, McManaman was top of the Premier League goal assists chart with 25 assists over the season,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> including assists and top ratings in <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C._4%E2%80%933_Newcastle_United_F.C._(1996)" title="Liverpool F.C. 4â3 Newcastle United F.C. (1996)">a match against Newcastle</a> voted the best of the decade in the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_10_Seasons_Awards" title="Premier League 10 Seasons Awards">Premier League 10 Seasons Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> By now, McManaman was ranked as one of the finest midfielders in England and had developed a strong reputation on the European stage following <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1996" title="UEFA Euro 1996">UEFA Euro 1996</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> earning praise from many at the time including <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Keegan" title="Kevin Keegan">Kevin Keegan</a>, who said "there are few finer sights in world football than the sight of Steve McManaman running down the length of the pitch."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>McManaman had also been noted for his versatility in his free role, switching from right to left wings, and his ability to play in central midfield, behind the front pair, or as a forward, with many notable managers including then <a href="/wiki/AFC_Ajax" title="AFC Ajax">Ajax</a> coach <a href="/wiki/Louis_van_Gaal" title="Louis van Gaal">Louis van Gaal</a>, describing it as a role few could pull off the way McManaman had.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> McManaman was credited for making the role manager Evans gave him work, with the result being that Liverpool were playing some of the most aesthetically pleasing attacking football at the time in England.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian.co.uk_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-guardian.co.uk-28">[28]</a></sup> McManaman was also said to have been one of only a handful of so-called "talismanic" players along with <a href="/wiki/Eric_Cantona" title="Eric Cantona">Eric Cantona</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gianfranco_Zola" title="Gianfranco Zola">Gianfranco Zola</a> in the league at the time believed to have the charisma to lift supporters from their seats each time they got the ball.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Managers would deploy a man-marker specifically to follow him for an entire game,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> with Gianfranco Zola noting that McManaman was the player the Italian national players monitored the most.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Howard_Wilkinson" title="Howard Wilkinson">Howard Wilkinson</a> said McManaman was "virtually unstoppable" at times,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> while then <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_F.C." title="Middlesbrough F.C.">Middlesbrough</a> manager, <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Robson" title="Bryan Robson">Bryan Robson</a>, was quoted as saying that "everyone in the Premiership knows that if you stop McManaman, you stop Liverpool."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> Roy Evans, attempting to diminish the attention on marking McManaman, stated "I would hate to think we are no more than a one-man team."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> German coach <a href="/wiki/Berti_Vogts" title="Berti Vogts">Berti Vogts</a> named McManaman as one of only three Premiership players in his select European XI Team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id=".22Spice_Boys.22">"Spice Boys"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steve_McManaman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title='Edit section: "Spice Boys"'>edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>However, things started to turn sour for McManaman and some of his team-mates. As their fame increased, <a href="/wiki/Tabloid_(newspaper_format)" title="Tabloid (newspaper format)">tabloid</a> newspaper stories of <a href="/wiki/Lad_culture" title="Lad culture">lad culture</a> excesses emerged and this, fused with underachievement on the pitch, brought criticism in the media. Defeat to <a href="/wiki/Alex_Ferguson" title="Alex Ferguson">Alex Ferguson</a>'s Manchester United in two title races including the <a href="/wiki/1996_FA_Cup_Final" title="1996 FA Cup Final">1996 FA Cup Final</a>, a game where the Liverpool team arrived to inspect the pitch wearing cream coloured <a href="/wiki/Armani" title="Armani">Armani</a> suits intensified the criticism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> McManaman and other teammates were reported to have cashed in on their newfound fame as stars of the nascent Premier League, to live a high life involving <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Groupies" title="Groupies">groupies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nightclub" title="Nightclub">clubbing</a> and other "high jinks". Modelling contracts and deals with fashion labels like <a href="/wiki/Topman" title="Topman">Top Man</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Boss" title="Hugo Boss">Hugo Boss</a> and <a href="/wiki/Armani" title="Armani">Armani</a> culminated in their collective nickname: '<a href="/wiki/Spice_Boys_(footballers)" title="Spice Boys (footballers)">The Spice Boys</a>.'<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> The situation was further aggravated by stories of McManaman and <a href="/wiki/Robbie_Fowler" title="Robbie Fowler">Robbie Fowler</a>'s lifestyles off the pitch following an interview with the magazine, <i><a href="/wiki/Loaded_(magazine)" title="Loaded (magazine)">Loaded</a></i>, which depicted the duo as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hedonists" title="Hedonists">hedonists</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Scallie&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Scallie (page does not exist)">scally</a> characters, as well as stories about McManaman and Fowler's lack of decorum and disruptive influence in the dressing room.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian.co.uk_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-guardian.co.uk-28">[28]</a></sup> McManaman responded by joining <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i> to write a weekly column, becoming the first footballer of his generation to do so.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>McManaman was also criticised for scoring too few goals, although he did make up for this with a formidable rate of assists for the likes of Fowler and later <a href="/wiki/Michael_Owen" title="Michael Owen">Michael Owen</a>, with Owen saying that "Liverpool at the time was built around McManaman"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> and was an average team whenever McManaman was not on form.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> The few goals that McManaman did score tended to be spectacular or memorable â most notably an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Injury_time" title="Injury time">injury time</a> solo goal against <a href="/wiki/Celtic_F.C." title="Celtic F.C.">Celtic</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup" title="UEFA Cup">UEFA Cup</a>, when McManaman scored after a 75-yard dribble. Other outstanding goals during his Liverpool career included goals against <a href="/wiki/Aston_Villa_F.C." title="Aston Villa F.C.">Aston Villa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a> and scoring the winner in a match against <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> with a stunning <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Volley_(football)" title="Volley (football)">volley</a>, after which he won a <a href="/wiki/Professional_Footballers%27_Association" title="Professional Footballers' Association">PFA</a> Player of the Month award in December 1997.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Contract_wrangles">Contract wrangles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steve_McManaman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Contract wrangles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In August 1997, Liverpool, having been unable to agree a new contract with McManaman and fearing that the player might leave on a <a href="/wiki/Bosman_ruling" title="Bosman ruling">Bosman free transfer</a>, accepted a Â£12 million bid for the player from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/F.C._Barcelona" title="F.C. Barcelona">Barcelona</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-44">[44]</a></sup> The deal subsequently fell apart amidst recriminations about the player's remuneration demands and Barcelona's motives for the bid, being in negotiation with <a href="/wiki/Rivaldo" title="Rivaldo">Rivaldo</a> at the same time and snubbing McManaman when he travelled to Spain to meet them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thefreelibrary.com_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-thefreelibrary.com-45">[45]</a></sup> By the end of the saga, the whole fiasco seemed to be a non-affair, with Barcelona signing Rivaldo after Sir <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Robson" title="Bobby Robson">Bobby Robson</a> intervened and told Van Gaal that McManaman was a cosmetic player who wouldn't score Barcelona 18 goals a season,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> while McManaman himself stated that he had no desire to leave Liverpool and with two years left on his contract was simply not in any rush to sign a new one.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> A subsequent bid of Â£11 million from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Juventus" title="Juventus">Juventus</a> in November of the same year was rejected by both club and player.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-espn.co.uk_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-espn.co.uk-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>McManaman was named Liverpool captain at the start of the <a href="/wiki/1998%E2%80%9399_in_English_football" title="1998â99 in English football">1998â99</a> season,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lfcp_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-lfcp-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-liverpoolfc.tv_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-liverpoolfc.tv-11">[11]</a></sup> but contract negotiations continued to flounder as the club could not match the sums available to McManaman if he left as a free agent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Having been overlooked by <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Hoddle" title="Glenn Hoddle">Glenn Hoddle</a> for the <a href="/wiki/1998_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1998 FIFA World Cup">1998 World Cup</a> squad in an underachieving Liverpool side,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> denounced in the English media as being greedy and bolstered by advice from the likes of fellow professionals <a href="/wiki/Paul_Ince" title="Paul Ince">Paul Ince</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Gascoigne" title="Paul Gascoigne">Paul Gascoigne</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Platt_(footballer)" title="David Platt (footballer)">David Platt</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chris_Waddle" title="Chris Waddle">Chris Waddle</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-madrid_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-madrid-52">[52]</a></sup> McManaman publicly announced his desire to play abroad.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>Numerous European clubs circled the soon-to-be free agent with <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid</a> quickly being seen as his most likely destination.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> In January 1999 it was reported that McManaman was talking to Real with the player reportedly offered Â£60,000 a week and nearly Â£2 million as a signing on fee.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> On 30 January, McManaman passed a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical" title="Medical">medical</a> and signed an official pre-contract with the club which would make him the best paid British footballer to date.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> He declined to pose in a Real Madrid shirt at the contract signing event, out of respect for Liverpool's fans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>McManaman's image of being a contract rebel and <a href="/wiki/Mercenary" title="Mercenary">mercenary</a> was exacerbated by his involvement in a year-long dispute between 1997 and 1998 with <a href="/wiki/Umbro" title="Umbro">Umbro</a>, his <a href="/wiki/Football_boot" title="Football boot">football boot</a> sponsor. Umbro sued him for <a href="/wiki/Breach_of_contract" title="Breach of contract">breach of contract</a> for knowingly wearing <a href="/wiki/Reebok" title="Reebok">Reebok</a> branded boots in contravention of the deal, and deliberately "blacking out" their <a href="/wiki/Logo" title="Logo">logo</a> on his boots in protest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> McManaman argued that his contract was unenforceable and an unlawful <a href="/wiki/Restraint_of_trade" title="Restraint of trade">restraint of trade</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> McManaman claimed that he was being exploited. He hired the services of agent <a href="/wiki/Simon_Fuller" title="Simon Fuller">Simon Fuller</a> to help free him from the sponsorship contract.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> The court initially ordered McManaman to fulfil his contract, plus an undertaking to pay Umbro's legal costs for launching <a href="/wiki/Contempt_of_court" title="Contempt of court">contempt of court</a> proceedings against him in 1997, which McManaman accepted and apologised for.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> A year on, however, McManaman continued to dishonour the deal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> He finally won an out-of-court <a href="/wiki/Settlement_(litigation)" title="Settlement (litigation)">settlement</a> in October 1998, freeing him to negotiate with other companies for what he regarded as remuneration appropriate to his status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> The case, in addition to his Liverpool contract wrangles saw the media describe McManaman as the "star performer in his own <a href="/wiki/Soap_opera" title="Soap opera">soap</a>",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-findarticles.com_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-findarticles.com-65">[65]</a></sup> though McManaman's Liverpool manager Roy Evans defended the player, stating: "Macca is so laid-back you would never know he was hurting inside. But he has been. Some of the criticisms have been so unfair. Typical of Macca, he's responded magnificently."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-findarticles.com_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-findarticles.com-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Departure">Departure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steve_McManaman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Departure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Having signed the pre-contract with Madrid, McManaman still had five months left on his contract at Liverpool. New manager <a href="/wiki/G%C3%A9rard_Houllier" title="GÃ©rard Houllier">GÃ©rard Houllier</a>, who had replaced Evans as full coach following the failure of their joint-managerial role, was widely believed to want to get rid of the "Spice Boys" mentality and cavalier attitudes at the club<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> having told many players they were surplus to requirements (including <a href="/wiki/Jason_McAteer" title="Jason McAteer">Jason McAteer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phil_Babb" title="Phil Babb">Phil Babb</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rob_Jones_(footballer_born_1971)" title="Rob Jones (footballer born 1971)">Rob Jones</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stig_Bjornebye" title="Stig Bjornebye">Stig Bjornebye</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paul_Ince" title="Paul Ince">Paul Ince</a>). While stating that he would have preferred that the player stayed, he said that the club had to respect McManaman's decision to exercise his right to leave at the end of his contract. Houllier said: "It wasn't unexpected. Steve had always maintained that he wanted to move abroad and I have to respect thatÂ ... Emotionally we will miss him because he's a Liverpool lad, and needless to say as a player you can't fault him because he has immense abilityÂ ... I will have to replace him, it's my job to go out and find another Steve McManaman.".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>In McManaman's final games for the club in the second half of the <a href="/wiki/1998%E2%80%9399_in_English_football" title="1998â99 in English football">1998â99</a> season, he began turning in mixed performances, with the media accusing him of playing out his final season in a "desultory manner".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> His form dipped at times, arguably due to a combination of injuries, being restricted to substitute appearances (as Houllier wanted to cut the side's dependency on his gameplay and replace him<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-3">[3]</a></sup>), and loss of confidence in certain games where even the home fans turned against him over the contract debacle, with some labelling him a 'traitor' and a <a href="/wiki/Judas_Iscariot" title="Judas Iscariot">Judas</a> figure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> McManaman told the media after one such game where he became victim of the "boo boys", saying: "That's understandable, when I came off the other day I knew the reaction there was going to be. But I think if they put themselves in the same predicament, and the fact that I have been at Liverpool for 12 years and that I would like to test myself in a foreign country, that's understandable." <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>McManaman also suffered personal tragedy when his mother Irene, who was bedridden with <a href="/wiki/Breast_cancer" title="Breast cancer">breast cancer</a> for two years, died during this time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>The combination of these factors meant McManaman suffered a loss of form, but, McManaman managed to rally and pick up his play right at the end of that last campaign. McManaman scored a crucial goal away at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blackburn_Rovers" title="Blackburn Rovers">Blackburn Rovers</a>, set up a dramatic injury time equaliser with a through ball for Paul Ince to score in front of the Kop against Manchester United,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> and scored the winner from outside the area with a half volley to complete the full turn around result against <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a>, after trailing 2â0 at half time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> In what was the final match of the season, and what would be McManaman's final match and final contribution on the pitch for the club, McManaman assisted <a href="/wiki/Karl-Heinz_Riedle" title="Karl-Heinz Riedle">Karl-Heinz Riedle</a> with a goal at the <a href="/wiki/Spion_Kop_(stadiums)" title="Spion Kop (stadiums)">Kop</a> with a trademark right wing run and pull back as Liverpool won 3â0 against <a href="/wiki/Wimbledon_F.C." title="Wimbledon F.C.">Wimbledon</a>, enabling McManaman to end his career at the club to a standing ovation, a lap of honour at Anfield,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> and a two row squad farewell at the entrance of the players' tunnel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Achievements">Achievements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steve_McManaman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Achievements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In spite of the side only winning two trophies during his time with Liverpool, McManaman's achievements at the club were exceptional for a player in a side often labelled negatively. McManaman finished alongside <a href="/wiki/Nick_Barmby" title="Nick Barmby">Nick Barmby</a> as joint runner up to Giggs in the <a href="/wiki/PFA_Young_Player_of_the_Year" title="PFA Young Player of the Year">PFA Young Player of the Year</a> awards in 1992,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> was named in the <a href="/wiki/PFA_Team_of_the_Year" title="PFA Team of the Year">PFA Team of the Year</a> for <a href="/wiki/PFA_Team_of_the_Year_(1990s)#FA_Premier_League_5" title="PFA Team of the Year (1990s)">1996â97</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> and also made the five man shortlist for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PFA_Player_of_the_Year" title="PFA Player of the Year">PFA Player of the Year</a> for three seasons from <a href="/wiki/1995%E2%80%9396_in_English_football" title="1995â96 in English football">1995â96</a> to <a href="/wiki/1997%E2%80%9398_in_English_football" title="1997â98 in English football">1997â98</a>, with the PFA website describing him as one of the most gifted players of his generation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wing_8-3"><a href="#cite_note-wing-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>For a time McManaman held the record for most consecutive Premier League appearances as an ever present at Liverpool for four seasons including a club record for most appearances, and at the time of leaving the Premiership had the second highest ratio of Premier League assists per game, with 112 assists in 272 appearances,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> with a total of 142 assists for the club;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> an average of one assist per two and a half games. As of 2011â12, McManaman holds the 14th position on the Premiership's All Time Assists charts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> Until 2011, McManaman held the record for greatest number of assists in Liverpool history, ahead of <a href="/wiki/Steven_Gerrard" title="Steven Gerrard">Steven Gerrard</a>, who has since overtaken him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> McManaman is also ranked 5th on the Premier League all-time assists charts for number of games it took to hit 100 assists, and also in terms of being the 5th youngest player to hit 100 assists in Premier League history, with only <a href="/wiki/Thierry_Henry" title="Thierry Henry">Thierry Henry</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cesc_Fabregas" title="Cesc Fabregas">Cesc Fabregas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Giggs" title="Ryan Giggs">Ryan Giggs</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_Beckham" title="David Beckham">David Beckham</a> above him in the list.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 5 September 2006, Steve McManaman was named #22 in the official Liverpool website's "100 Players Who Shook The Kop" list,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> in which <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Carragher" title="Jamie Carragher">Jamie Carragher</a> described McManaman as "the best midfield player in the country for three or four years" running.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-liverpoolfc.tv_11-3"><a href="#cite_note-liverpoolfc.tv-11">[11]</a></sup> Both <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rob_Jones_(footballer_born_1971)" title="Rob Jones (footballer born 1971)">Rob Jones</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> and Robbie Fowler gave two interviews in 2012â13 in which they stated McManaman was the greatest player they ever played alongside,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> with Fowler saying: "I've played with many, many great players. Paul Gascoigne was fantastic and I could sit here all day and talk about Liverpool players - John Barnes, Ian Rush, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jan_Molby" title="Jan Molby">Jan Molby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ronnie_Whelan" title="Ronnie Whelan">Ronnie Whelan</a> and Steven Gerrard, who is an unbelievable player. He would probably be my number two. The best player I've ever played with is Steve McManamanÂ ... he really was that good."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> In 2013, McManaman was named #20 in the official Liverpool website's second "100 Players Who Shook the Kop" list, rising up by two positions.</p>
<p>When <a href="/wiki/Mark_Lawrenson" title="Mark Lawrenson">Mark Lawrenson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jim_Beglin" title="Jim Beglin">Jim Beglin</a> named McManaman in their team of the 1990s, they said that most managers in the league used the same tactic of marking McManaman to stop Liverpool and whilst it was a tremendous compliment to McManaman,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> the opposition could stop Liverpool because the tactical system of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/3-5-2" title="3-5-2">3-5-2</a> or 3-4-1-2 was too dependent on McManaman and would fail if McManaman was off form, or if the team was not complemented by a quality defence (players who could play both wingback and centre half to cope with onslaughts), or the presence of a steely defensive midfielder, which was what happened with the team of that time. Nevertheless, McManaman was voted in on the official Liverpool FC website as the club's midfielder of the 1990s,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> was named by <a href="/wiki/Ruud_Gullit" title="Ruud Gullit">Ruud Gullit</a> as one of his top two players from the entire Premier League era,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> and despite Liverpool fans' disappointment over the nature of how McManaman conducted his departure, it is believed that many fans still regard McManaman (along with Fowler) as the two players who carried Liverpool through the 1990s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2012, as part of the FA <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_20_Seasons_Awards" title="Premier League 20 Seasons Awards">Premier League 20 Seasons Awards</a>, Steve McManaman was named on the shortlist for the award of best right midfielder,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> which was eventually won by <a href="/wiki/Cristiano_Ronaldo" title="Cristiano Ronaldo">Cristiano Ronaldo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Real_Madrid">Real Madrid</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steve_McManaman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Real Madrid">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_success">Early success</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steve_McManaman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Early success">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 1 July 1999, after 364 appearances and 66 goals for Liverpool, McManaman transferred to Real Madrid as <a href="/wiki/Guus_Hiddink" title="Guus Hiddink">Guus Hiddink</a>'s last signing<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> (before being sacked, and while the club was under President <a href="/wiki/Lorenzo_Sanz" title="Lorenzo Sanz">Lorenzo Sanz</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> Before McManaman arrived, the club was described as undergoing a management and <a href="/wiki/Debt" title="Debt">debt</a> crisis and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ra%C3%BAl_Gonz%C3%A1lez" title="RaÃºl GonzÃ¡lez">RaÃºl GonzÃ¡lez</a> told the press: "The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dressing_room" title="Dressing room">dressing room</a> is a cesspit of lies, treachery and whispersÂ ... I feel sorry for new players like Steve McManaman coming into the club. If McManaman thinks he is coming to one of the world's top clubs then he has made a big mistake."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> The club appointed <a href="/wiki/John_Toshack" title="John Toshack">John Toshack</a> as its new coach and had already been forced to sell key players like <a href="/wiki/Predrag_Mijatovi%C4%87" title="Predrag MijatoviÄ">Predrag MijatoviÄ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Davor_%C5%A0uker" title="Davor Å uker">Davor Å uker</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christian_Panucci" title="Christian Panucci">Christian Panucci</a> due to mounting debt, while <a href="/wiki/Clarence_Seedorf" title="Clarence Seedorf">Clarence Seedorf</a> was also released shortly after McManaman arrived.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> McManaman's arrival saw him become only the second English player to ever play for the club, after <a href="/wiki/Laurie_Cunningham" title="Laurie Cunningham">Laurie Cunningham</a> had played for them in the 1980s. He was also the most high-profile English footballer to move to <a href="/wiki/La_Liga" title="La Liga">Spanish</a> football since <a href="/wiki/Gary_Lineker" title="Gary Lineker">Gary Lineker</a> had moved to <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">FC Barcelona</a> from Everton in 1986. Thereafter he proved an instant hit with the fans at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santiago_Bernab%C3%A9u_stadium" title="Santiago BernabÃ©u stadium">Santiago BernabÃ©u stadium</a> after scoring three times and creating several goals in his first few games for <i>Los Merengues</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wright_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-wright-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<p>McManaman made his debut for Madrid on 22 August 1999 in the 2â1 <a href="/wiki/La_Liga" title="La Liga">La Liga</a> win over <a href="/wiki/RCD_Mallorca" title="RCD Mallorca">RCD Mallorca</a> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ONO_Estadi" title="ONO Estadi">Son Moix</a> stadium, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mallorca" title="Mallorca">Mallorca</a>, where he assisted <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Morientes" title="Fernando Morientes">Fernando Morientes</a> in scoring the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Injury_time" title="Injury time">injury time</a> winner. He scored his first goal for the club a week later on his home debut on 29 August, in a 4â1 thumping of <a href="/wiki/CD_Numancia" title="CD Numancia">Numancia</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Bernab%C3%A9u_Stadium" title="Santiago BernabÃ©u Stadium">BernabÃ©u</a>.</p>
<p>In December 1999 to January 2000, McManaman and the Madrid team took part in the controversial inaugural <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FIFA_Club_World_Championship" title="FIFA Club World Championship">FIFA Club World Championships</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a>, where McManaman missed an injury time chance to win the game, and then the <a href="/wiki/Penalty_kick_(association_football)" title="Penalty kick (association football)">penalty kick</a> against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Necaxa" title="Necaxa">Necaxa</a> that would have sent Madrid into 3rd place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> McManaman and the team then returned to Spain and established themselves as the side that went all the way to the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> Final in 2000, under new coach <a href="/wiki/Vicente_del_Bosque" title="Vicente del Bosque">Vicente del Bosque</a>, who had replaced <a href="/wiki/John_Toshack" title="John Toshack">John Toshack</a> in November. McManaman's form in the buildup saw him receive several man of the match awards, forming a strong midfield partnership with <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Redondo" title="Fernando Redondo">Fernando Redondo</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> as Madrid beat holders <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manchester_United" title="Manchester United">Manchester United</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bayern_Munich" title="Bayern Munich">Bayern Munich</a> to reach the final.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> It was at this <a href="/wiki/2000_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2000 UEFA Champions League Final">2000 UEFA Champions League Final</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Stade_de_France" title="Stade de France">Stade de France</a> in Paris that McManaman experienced his finest hour as a player â scoring a spectacular volley in a 3â0 victory over fellow Spanish side <a href="/wiki/Valencia_CF" title="Valencia CF">Valencia</a>. His performance on this greatest of club football stages saw him hailed the man of the match by the English press,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> a view endorsed by his Madrid team-mate <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ivan_Helguera" title="Ivan Helguera">Ivan Helguera</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-independent.co.uk_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-independent.co.uk-106">[106]</a></sup> His part in Madrid's eighth European Cup win saw him become the first English player ever to win Europe's premier club competition with a foreign club.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2000.2F01_Season">2000/01 Season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steve_McManaman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 2000/01 Season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Despite that European Cup Final performance and having established himself as a valuable player in his first year in Madrid, the arrival of a new President in <a href="/wiki/Florentino_P%C3%A9rez" title="Florentino PÃ©rez">Florentino PÃ©rez</a>, closely followed by former Barcelona superstar midfielder <a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_Figo" title="LuÃ­s Figo">LuÃ­s Figo</a>, in a club record transfer, saw the club forced to sell several key players to reduce debt. <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Redondo" title="Fernando Redondo">Fernando Redondo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Anelka" title="Nicolas Anelka">Nicolas Anelka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christian_Karembeu" title="Christian Karembeu">Christian Karembeu</a> and McManaman were suddenly told they were surplus to requirements before the start of the 2000â01 season and were sold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> When McManaman refused to leave unlike the others, manager Del Bosque told McManaman that he had "little chance of playing this year,"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> and in case he didn't understand his position, the club also declined to give him a squad number for the forthcoming season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-forbes.com_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-forbes.com-109">[109]</a></sup> With the club already in debt, and having just spent another Â£37m on Figo, the board were keen to cash in on McManaman and remove his $4.5m salary from the wage bill.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-forbes.com_109-1"><a href="#cite_note-forbes.com-109">[109]</a></sup> McManaman, however, with an iron-clad contract until 2004, declined to leave and instead stated his determination to win back his place in the team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-independent.co.uk_106-1"><a href="#cite_note-independent.co.uk-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<p>Real Madrid subsequently accepted first an <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">Â£</a>11 million bid from <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_F.C." title="Middlesbrough F.C.">Middlesbrough</a> and then a Â£12 million bid for McManaman from <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> that included the exchange of <a href="/wiki/Tore_Andr%C3%A9_Flo" title="Tore AndrÃ© Flo">Tore AndrÃ© Flo</a>, in the summer of 2000, both of which the player rejected. A <a href="/wiki/Sky_Sports" title="Sky Sports">Sky Sports</a> report in August 2000 also stated that eight other clubs were racing for his signature at the time, including Manchester United, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parma_F.C." title="Parma F.C.">Parma</a> and <a href="/wiki/ACF_Fiorentina" title="ACF Fiorentina">Fiorentina</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> but McManaman remained adamant even as Sir Alex Ferguson also declared his admiration for McManaman by arranging a contingent to convince him to sign<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> but McManaman said he wanted to succeed in Spain. His stance was rewarded when Real relented after a Spanish poll in <i><a href="/wiki/El_Mundo_(Spain)" title="El Mundo (Spain)">El Mundo</a></i> showed 90% of the fans demanded the club keep McManaman, while <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Michel_Salgado" title="Michel Salgado">Michel Salgado</a> complained to the management about the way McManaman was treated after McManaman turned down yet again, another transfer attempt- this time to <a href="/wiki/Lazio" title="Lazio">Lazio</a>, who came in with an Â£8 million offer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> Real's change toward McManaman began when Del Bosque gave him his first appearance of the 2000â01 season as a substitute in a 3â3 draw against <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1laga_CF" title="MÃ¡laga CF">MÃ¡laga</a> in September.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> McManaman reportedly won over the manager by October, and managed to feature in two thirds of the club's matches, becoming a first team regular for the second half of the campaign, and held the unique distinction of being described as the only top class football player from England playing overseas at the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> McManaman shone in this second season at Madrid as his club side challenged for the La Liga title and Champions League- where they lost in the semi-finals to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bayern_Munich" title="Bayern Munich">Bayern Munich</a>, but won their 28th La Liga crown by a seven-point margin over the previous seasons champions, <a href="/wiki/Deportivo_de_La_Coru%C3%B1a" title="Deportivo de La CoruÃ±a">Deportivo La CoruÃ±a</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wright_100-1"><a href="#cite_note-wright-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Gal.C3.A1cticos_policy"><i>GalÃ¡cticos</i> policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steve_McManaman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: GalÃ¡cticos policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>McManaman increasingly saw his playing time reduced each year, as the club initiated their now well known <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gal%C3%A1ctico" title="GalÃ¡ctico">GalÃ¡ctico</a></i> policy, with world class names like <a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_Figo" title="LuÃ­s Figo">LuÃ­s Figo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zinedine_Zidane" title="Zinedine Zidane">Zinedine Zidane</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ronaldo_(Brazilian_footballer)" title="Ronaldo (Brazilian footballer)">Ronaldo</a> arriving each year and standing above him in the pecking order. At the time though, McManaman was known for his dogged determination to stay positive for the club's cause, even if it meant he had less playing time. In 2002, McManaman also turned down a transfer to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/F.C._Internazionale_Milano" title="F.C. Internazionale Milano">Internazionale</a> at the time when he was made available for exchange as part of Ronaldo's signing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> It was widely reported in the Spanish media that McManaman's resilience to the team won the respect of his fellow professionals like <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ra%C3%BAl_Gonz%C3%A1lez" title="RaÃºl GonzÃ¡lez">RaÃºl</a>, Zidane, <a href="/wiki/Guti_(footballer)" title="Guti (footballer)">Guti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iv%C3%A1n_Helguera" title="IvÃ¡n Helguera">IvÃ¡n Helguera</a>, and his two best friends and <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">golf</a> buddies at the club, Figo and Ronaldo,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> who backed him publicly on several occasions in press interviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> McManaman was also twice voted as the Real Madrid supporters' favourite player at the club during his tenure,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> who adored him for his workrate,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> and where the Spanish media would rave about him regarding anything from his love of the Madrid lifestyle, his willingness to learn the language and immerse into their culture,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> to his home in La Moraleja, or even his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Androgynous" title="Androgynous">androgynous</a> <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/resemblance" title="wikt:resemblance">resemblance</a> to <a href="/wiki/Hollywood" title="Hollywood">Hollywood</a> actress <a href="/wiki/Nicole_Kidman" title="Nicole Kidman">Nicole Kidman</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> all of which, curiously resulted in bolstering his "affable and amiable" image as the darling of the team at that time. According to <i><a href="/wiki/El_Pa%C3%ADs" title="El PaÃ­s">El PaÃ­s</a></i>, in 2001, fans saluted him with their 'white handkerchiefs' (as a terrace favourite) after he acrobatically scored a 'wonder goal' (an incredible long-range high volley) against <a href="/wiki/Real_Oviedo" title="Real Oviedo">Real Oviedo</a> that year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<p>McManaman also forced himself to reinvent his game, and transform himself with a versatility that enabled him to play utility roles in the side, thus helping him shake off a derogatory nickname he was initially given by the Spanish Press, "El Cartero" (the postman)- the implication being that though he could dribble long distances, he seemed to collect the ball and deliver it who knows where, in the manner of the Spanish postal service.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> It was widely regarded as a credit to McManaman that he managed to constantly reinvent himself to be effective and useful in a squad that was widely regarded at the time as the "best team in the world" under the "Galaticos" policy.</p>
<p>Yet the policy had its detractors, and according to certain critics in the Spanish press, McManaman and several other players became "victims" as the policy was based more on marketing and revenue generation, and sometimes meant players were picked not according to form, but because of their money-making potential off the pitch. To his credit, McManaman never spoke ill of the <i>GalÃ¡ctico</i> policy's effects on him during his tenure, only critiquing the policy and ultimately describing it in his <a href="/wiki/Autobiography" title="Autobiography">autobiography</a> "El Macca" (a book that was shortlisted as the <a href="/wiki/William_Hill_Sports_Book_of_the_Year" title="William Hill Sports Book of the Year">William Hill Sports Book of the Year</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> in 2004 as the "<a href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Company" title="The Walt Disney Company">Disneyfication</a> of Real Madrid" upon his departure from the club; a piece of foresight that proved telling for the future as the club never reached its heights in the period ensuing with the policy, and with the term becoming somewhat pejorative to this day.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_Champions_League">Second Champions League</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steve_McManaman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Second Champions League">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Eventually, the Board, including <a href="/wiki/Florentino_P%C3%A9rez" title="Florentino PÃ©rez">Florentino PÃ©rez</a> relented, declaring that a "man like that would always have a place in my club", adding that "McManaman is in now in the team because his behaviour has been in accordance with the true values of the club." <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Johan_Cruyff" title="Johan Cruyff">Johan Cruyff</a> meanwhile, described McManaman at the time as the most useful player in the "Galaticos" because he was "everyone's best partner on the pitch."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> A further honour was also extended on the pitch by the club in the 2001â02 season, whereas part of Madrid's Centenary Celebrations, McManaman was made the first Englishman to captain Real Madrid in a game against a <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> World XI, to the applause of the <a href="/wiki/Ultras" title="Ultras">ultras</a>, with whom he was a cult favourite.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> Arguably his second greatest moment in the white of Madrid also took place that year, in the 2002 UEFA Champions League semi-final against <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">Barcelona</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Camp_Nou" title="Camp Nou">Camp Nou</a> on 23 April 2002. In this match of monumental proportions, due to "El ClÃ¡sico" being a massive game in its own right, but also the fact that it was a <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> Semi-final, McManaman appeared as a second-half substitute to score a critical goal in second half injury time to secure a 2â0 first-leg advantage, chipping over goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Bonano" title="Roberto Bonano">Roberto Bonano</a> after being played in by <a href="/wiki/Fl%C3%A1vio_Concei%C3%A7%C3%A3o" title="FlÃ¡vio ConceiÃ§Ã£o">FlÃ¡vio ConceiÃ§Ã£o</a>, after Zidane had scored the first goal on 55 minutes. This notable victory, Real's first at the Camp Nou since 1993, helped secure their place in the final of the 2002 Champions League at <a href="/wiki/Hampden_Park" title="Hampden Park">Hampden Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a>, where he came on as a replacement for Figo â and thereby ensuring his second Champions League winners' medal, after Madrid secured a 2â1 victory over German team <a href="/wiki/Bayer_04_Leverkusen" title="Bayer 04 Leverkusen">Bayer Leverkusen</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wright_100-2"><a href="#cite_note-wright-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Final_season">Final season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steve_McManaman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Final season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>McManaman was used as a late substitute for games at the start of the campaign and after scoring a goal and assisting in several of new signing Ronaldo's goals,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> he was given surprise starts. In one of his starts, he scored a brace against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AEK_Athens" title="AEK Athens">AEK Athens</a> in the Champions' league. McManaman also started in a famous game in 2003, where Madrid were beaten 4â3 at <a href="/wiki/Old_Trafford" title="Old Trafford">Old Trafford</a> in the Champions' League, even as Ronaldo hit a hat-trick.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> Nonetheless, after only playing 21 games of which he started only 9 times, and making a meagre 15 appearances in La Liga, questions constantly arose throughout the season about McManaman's ability and reasons for staying in Spain considering his diminished role, lack of first team action and international attention. Suggestions that McManaman had "sold out" for money and had grown indifferent and lackadaisical to his football were rampant in the British Press, though the media were also described as suffering from "a selective media amnesia over McManaman's time in Spain."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> Nonetheless, McManaman managed to pick up a second La Liga medal for the year, and was in the squad that won the <a href="/wiki/Intercontinental_Cup_(football)" title="Intercontinental Cup (football)">Intercontinental Cup</a> in Japan.</p>
<p>At the start of the 2003â04 pre-season, the signing of fellow Englishman <a href="/wiki/David_Beckham" title="David Beckham">David Beckham</a> proved the last straw in eventually forcing McManaman down the pecking order at Real Madrid. McManaman remained with the club for its full pre-season, even after coach Del Bosque was given a shock sacking 24 hours after having won the club's last La liga title,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> but in the close season, and the arrival of <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Queiroz" title="Carlos Queiroz">Carlos Queiroz</a> as new coach, McManaman was released by the club after helping Beckham settle in with the language and despite Beckham's pleas to the management for McManaman to remain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy_at_Madrid">Legacy at Madrid</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steve_McManaman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Legacy at Madrid">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Having won 8 trophies and having played in 11 cup finals in four years as well as constantly making the semi-finals of the UEFA Champions league in each of his four years at the club, McManaman became the most successful English football export to ever play overseas (not just in Spain) in terms of trophies. In addition to honours, according to <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> magazine in 2001, McManaman was listed as 6th on the list of the highest earning footballers in the world,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> and is believed to have pocketed anywhere between an estimated 15 million Euros (just under Â£10,250,000) to Â£14,000,000 in his four years with Madrid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a tribute to McManaman, four years after he left the club, ex-coach Del Bosque told Spanish newspaper <i>AS Marca</i>, that McManaman and <a href="/wiki/Geremi_Njitap" title="Geremi Njitap">Geremi Njitap</a> were the two most important players in his squad, because "together they kept the whole team united."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> Del Bosque added: "I was very happy with Macca. He was a caballero, a gentleman, a stupendous guy; he always had a smile, he never complained, he was great, a leader. He related to everyone very well; he united people. He had a bad time [towards the end] with <a href="/wiki/Achilles" title="Achilles">achilles</a> pain, but every day he trained with the same attitude. He was exemplary ... and a good footballer too, very good. A fantastic player in every sense."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
<p>McManaman is also listed as a club legend on the official Real Madrid website, with his legacy being that of being fondly remembered as 'The versatile Englishman', and described as one who: "in only four seasons, won the hearts of Madrid's followers. The mixture of his gentlemanly nature both on and off the pitch, combined with teamwork and quality made sure that this Englishman was one of the most loved players by the fans...McManaman's natural position was on the right, but during his time at Real Madrid he played in every midfield position. His ability to change position made him a very versatile player."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
<p>McManaman also paved the way and influenced other British players to join Madrid in the ensuing years, with players such as Owen saying they asked him for advice before signing with Madrid,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> and later encouraged <a href="/wiki/Gareth_Bale" title="Gareth Bale">Gareth Bale</a> to sign for Madrid a decade later,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> going so far as to even declare that Bale "needed the Madrid move" on Real's official <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> account.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> When Bale signed, McManaman gave Bale advice on how to succeed at Madrid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> Bale would later become the first player to emulate McManaman when he ended up winning the UEFA Champions League with Madrid in his first season, something McManaman was delighted with, and expected all along.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup></p>
<p>McManaman was also listed in Spanish-based British sports reporter, <a href="/wiki/Sid_Lowe" title="Sid Lowe">Sid Lowe</a>'s Real Madrid Team of the Decade for the 2000s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Manchester_City">Manchester City</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steve_McManaman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Manchester City">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2003â04, along with teammates <a href="/wiki/Claude_Mak%C3%A9l%C3%A9l%C3%A9" title="Claude MakÃ©lÃ©lÃ©">Claude MakÃ©lÃ©lÃ©</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Hierro" title="Fernando Hierro">Fernando Hierro</a> and later <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Morientes" title="Fernando Morientes">Fernando Morientes</a>, McManaman headed back to the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a>. Initially reported to be joining <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> or <a href="/wiki/Everton_F.C." title="Everton F.C.">Everton</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> McManaman eventually decided to join long-time admirer <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Keegan" title="Kevin Keegan">Kevin Keegan</a> on 30 August at <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a>, resulting in a reunion with several ex-colleagues including <a href="/wiki/Robbie_Fowler" title="Robbie Fowler">Robbie Fowler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Anelka" title="Nicolas Anelka">Nicolas Anelka</a>, and later, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/David_James_(footballer)" title="David James (footballer)">David James</a>, prompting the media to state that Keegan was "reuniting the Spice Boys".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup></p>
<p>McManaman made his debut on 14 September 2003 in a 4â1 win over <a href="/wiki/Aston_Villa_F.C." title="Aston Villa F.C.">Aston Villa</a> at the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Manchester_Stadium" title="City of Manchester Stadium">City of Manchester Stadium</a>, and quickly showed good early form,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> with the club starting with a run of wins<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-search.japantimes.co.jp_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-search.japantimes.co.jp-153">[153]</a></sup> and progressing in the UEFA Cup,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> with McManaman hailed by Keegan to great hype, but by <a href="/wiki/Christmas" title="Christmas">Christmas</a> that year, results had fallen, the team languished<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> and ended the season, well out of European contention, and McManaman injured again. By 2004â05, McManaman's time at City was ultimately deemed a disappointment and he was increasingly vilified by the City fans,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> who later jeered him off the pitch following a draw with <a href="/wiki/Norwich_City_F.C." title="Norwich City F.C.">Norwich City</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> Fans also nicknamed him "McMoneyman" pejoratively in reference to old quibs about his reasons for leaving Liverpool, staying in Spain and picking City.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup></p>
<p>On the pitch, a combination of niggling injuries, and the rise of an in-form and up-and-coming <a href="/wiki/Shaun_Wright-Phillips" title="Shaun Wright-Phillips">Shaun Wright-Phillips</a> saw him lose his preferred right midfield position. When McManaman did play, he failed to rediscover his old form and speed, only occasionally demonstrating the ability he had shown in his earlier career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> Part of the problem stemmed from the fact that in order to find a role at Madrid he had changed his playing style, cutting down on the flair play (as Madrid had a surfeit of flair players) and instead focusing on being a holding player and making short, simple passes of the ball in central midfield, where he was known for his one touch passing and ability to never give the ball away.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wright_100-3"><a href="#cite_note-wright-100">[100]</a></sup> Youngsters Wright-Phillips, <a href="/wiki/Joey_Barton" title="Joey Barton">Joey Barton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Ireland" title="Stephen Ireland">Stephen Ireland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lee_Croft" title="Lee Croft">Lee Croft</a> cited McManaman as a major motivating influence on them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> McManaman was criticised by Alex Ferguson after an FA Cup <a href="/wiki/Manchester_derby" title="Manchester derby">Manchester derby</a> at Old Trafford for "intimidating <a href="/wiki/Gary_Neville" title="Gary Neville">Gary Neville</a>" to get him sent off in a <a href="/wiki/Headbutt" title="Headbutt">headbutt</a> incident in 2004, adding a derogatory comment that he had no idea what other role McManaman had in the game [and possibly for Manchester City].<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup></p>
<p>Off the field at City, Fowler and McManaman were caught up in a <a href="/wiki/Sex_scandal" title="Sex scandal">sex scandal</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> that appeared in the <i><a href="/wiki/News_of_the_World" title="News of the World">News of the World</a></i> following a failed attempt by the pair to gain an injunction to prevent publication- costing them Â£50,000 in addition to making the case look like an invariable admission of guilt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> The court case came fast on the heels of football's "<a href="/wiki/Roasting" title="Roasting">roasting</a>" and <a href="/wiki/Rape" title="Rape">rape</a> allegations at <a href="/wiki/Chelsea,_London" title="Chelsea, London">Chelsea</a> earlier that year<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> and served only to exacerbate their situations and affected their reputations off and on the pitch at the club, while an incident involving Fowler and McManaman and three other players deliberately missing the team bus at <a href="/wiki/Leicester" title="Leicester">Leicester</a> also did not go down well with the fans, manager and media.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2004, McManaman was linked to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MetroStars" title="MetroStars">MetroStars</a>, who confirmed that the club were interested in him. However they eventually decided to relinquish their bid stating that "<a href="/wiki/Major_League_Soccer" title="Major League Soccer">MLS</a> clubs were keen to lose the reputation that top stars only arrive to play in America for a final swansong in their careers".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> McManaman played for City for only two seasons and following Kevin Keegan's resignation in March 2005, never played another game for the club. Keegan's replacement, <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Pearce" title="Stuart Pearce">Stuart Pearce</a>, released McManaman on a free transfer on 20 May.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup></p>
<p>Though McManaman failed to score a single goal for City, his earlier successes enabled him to end his career across all his three clubs with a total of 560 appearances, scoring 80 goals,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> and with 182 assists; 142 of those notably coming in his time at Liverpool.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_career">International career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steve_McManaman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: International career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>For <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a>, McManaman would forever remain an enigma at international level. England coaches, except for Venables and Keegan, utilised McManaman's talents sparingly. McManaman was capped 37 times for England scoring three goals, and with the side only losing three times in the games that he played;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thefa.com_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-thefa.com-170">[170]</a></sup> two of them significant results- the infamous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euro_96" title="Euro 96">Euro 96</a> penalty shootout defeat to Germany at <a href="/wiki/Wembley" title="Wembley">Wembley</a> in 1996, and the opening day defeat against Portugal in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euro_2000" title="Euro 2000">Euro 2000</a>.</p>
