<p>Those European Championships in the Netherlands and Belgium were McManaman's last major tournament for England, despite backing from the press, fans and teammates including Zinedine Zidane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="England_U21">England U21</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steve_McManaman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: England U21">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>McManaman made history by becoming the first player without first team experience to play for the <a href="/wiki/England_national_under-21_football_team" title="England national under-21 football team">England Under-21</a> team, being handed a debut call-up by <a href="/wiki/Lawrie_McMenemy" title="Lawrie McMenemy">Lawrie McMenemy</a> against <a href="/wiki/Wales_national_under-21_football_team" title="Wales national under-21 football team">Wales</a> at <a href="/wiki/Prenton_Park" title="Prenton Park">Tranmere</a> in October 1990, two months before he debuted for the Liverpool first-team, famously quoting in the process that he had seen "more fat on a chip" in reference to McManaman's <a href="/wiki/Underweight" title="Underweight">skinny</a> physique.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wing_8-4"><a href="#cite_note-wing-8">[8]</a></sup> In February 1993, McManaman captained the <a href="/wiki/England_national_under-21_football_team" title="England national under-21 football team">England Under-21 team</a> for the first time against <a href="/wiki/San_Marino_national_under-21_football_team" title="San Marino national under-21 football team">San Marino</a> and scored the last goal in a convincing 6â0 win.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terry_Venables_and_Euro_96">Terry Venables and Euro 96</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steve_McManaman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Terry Venables and Euro 96">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Terry_Venables" title="Terry Venables">Terry Venables</a> gave McManaman his full debut on 16 November 1994 in an international friendly with <a href="/wiki/Nigeria_national_football_team" title="Nigeria national football team">Nigeria</a> at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley</a>, McManaman coming on as a replacement for <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Rob_Lee" title="Rob Lee">Robert Lee</a>. By 1995, McManaman was accused of struggling to repeat his fine club form with his country, drawing comparisons to his mentor at Liverpool, <a href="/wiki/John_Barnes_(footballer)" title="John Barnes (footballer)">John Barnes</a>. However, he managed to string together a series of splendid match winning performances for his country in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1996_UEFA_European_Football_Championship" title="1996 UEFA European Football Championship">Euro 96</a>, earning praise from even <a href="/wiki/Pel%C3%A9" title="PelÃ©">PelÃ©</a>, who according to the BBC, touted him as the tournament's best player and said he was the player he "was most impressed" by<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> going on to say that he was "one of the best players in Europe" and could be the "best in the world",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thefa.com_170-1"><a href="#cite_note-thefa.com-170">[170]</a></sup> tags that McManaman later admitted that he could not live up to. Together with team mates <a href="/wiki/David_Seaman" title="David Seaman">David Seaman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alan_Shearer" title="Alan Shearer">Alan Shearer</a>, McManaman was also listed in the official Team of the Tournament, as well as shortlisted behind eventual winner, <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCrgen_Klinsmann" title="JÃ¼rgen Klinsmann">JÃ¼rgen Klinsmann</a>, for the Most Valuable Player award.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Glenn_Hoddle_and_World_Cup_98">Glenn Hoddle and World Cup 98</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steve_McManaman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Glenn Hoddle and World Cup 98">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>However, McManaman failed to win over new England coach <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Hoddle" title="Glenn Hoddle">Glenn Hoddle</a> despite being in excellent club form in the years Hoddle was in charge,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> raising questions about either his effort, his attitude, or his relationship with the manager, with some sections of the British press even lobbying Hoddle to pick McManaman. Hoddle stated in interviews that he wanted McManaman to take up the licence to be the bridge between David Beckham and Paul Gascoigne,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> and often spoke highly of McManaman's ability, but noted that McManaman's best position was "floating" dangerously and it was hard to fit him into a system to suit the team<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> and so he often selected <a href="/wiki/Paul_Merson" title="Paul Merson">Paul Merson</a> and the rising Beckham instead. When McManaman (and Fowler) opted out of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Le_Tournoi" title="Le Tournoi">Le Tournoi</a> in 1997 to choose to undergo non-urgent medical operations ahead of International duty, it was noted that this reportedly lost them their team spots as Hoddle though angered at losing them, found a winning team in their absence, and this made it even harder for McManaman to regain his place later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> McManaman made a grand total of four appearances under Hoddle,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> and only one appearance at the <a href="/wiki/1998_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1998 FIFA World Cup">1998 FIFA World Cup</a> against <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>, as a substitute for <a href="/wiki/Paul_Scholes" title="Paul Scholes">Paul Scholes</a>. When interviewed by <a href="/wiki/FourFourTwo" title="FourFourTwo">FourFourTwo</a> magazine, McManaman stated: "I think I probably least enjoyed my time when Glenn Hoddle was the manager. But I wouldn't say he was necessarily the worst. He had his ways of training and ways of acting and all managers have different ways of doing things; it's the same with club managers. Sometimes when you join up with England and you don't play as often as you did under a certain other manager â then you'll think it's terrible. I loved going to play with England. For instance, I did get to go to the World Cup even though I only played for 17 minutes. That kind of experience leaves an indelible mark on your mind. So I don't really think of it in terms of "worst"; but going to the World Cup and not playing much was a big thing for me, really, and that was under Glenn, of course."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fourfourtwo.com_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-fourfourtwo.com-179">[179]</a></sup> Hoddle also notably arranged for McManaman to meet a disabled fan (and thus fulfill his lifelong wish of meeting McManaman) whilst the fan was on the verge of death, in 1997, to great media acclaim,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> though the story only broke a year after Hoddle had been sacked from the England job for alleged disparaging comments about disabled people.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kevin_Keegan_and_Euro_2000">Kevin Keegan and Euro 2000</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steve_McManaman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Kevin Keegan and Euro 2000">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Kevin Keegan quickly reinstated McManaman to the England <a href="/wiki/Starting_lineup" title="Starting lineup">starting lineup</a> after coming on the job. John Barnes spoke about McManaman in his autobiography in 1999 as "probably the greatest individual talent in English football and has to be presented the correct way",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> and Keegan gave several interviews in 1999 backing up that point; adding that he was finding out how best to utilise McManaman. Keegan eventually decided on deploying McManaman on the left wing on several occasions in 1999<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> and under Keegan, McManaman finally broke his international goal scoring duck, when he scored twice on 4 September 1999 in the 6â0 <a href="/wiki/UEFA_European_Championship" title="UEFA European Championship">Euro 2000</a> qualifier victory over <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_national_football_team" title="Luxembourg national football team">Luxembourg</a>, again, at Wembley. Keegan took McManaman's new career at Madrid to reinstate his confidence in him, and handed him a coveted free role ahead of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2000_UEFA_European_Football_Championship" title="2000 UEFA European Football Championship">Euro 2000</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> stating that "in the past we compromised himÂ ... but [following McManaman's UEFA Champions League success], we said 'we'll fit in with you, you've earned that chance'<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> McManaman played only once in Euro 2000, where he scored the last of his three England goals in a famous opening game against <a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_football_team" title="Portugal national football team">Portugal</a>, where McManaman put England 2â0 ahead, only for it to end because McManaman got injured after scoring, forcing a tactical switch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> McManaman never played for Keegan again as Keegan left the England job two months later in October 2000.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-2001_omission">Post-2001 omission</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steve_McManaman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Post-2001 omission">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The last of McManaman's caps came in 2001 when <a href="/wiki/Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson" title="Sven-GÃ¶ran Eriksson">Sven-GÃ¶ran Eriksson</a> utilised him for his first games in the <a href="/wiki/2002_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2002 FIFA World Cup">2002 FIFA World Cup</a> qualifiers, including a game back at Anfield against Finland â where McManaman set up David Beckham's winner<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup>â but then apparently left a message on McManaman's <a href="/wiki/Answering_machine" title="Answering machine">answering machine</a> to inform him that he was not going to be in the final <a href="/wiki/2002_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2002 FIFA World Cup">2002 FIFA World Cup</a> England squad in early 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> Despite the pleas of McManaman's Real Madrid team mates Zidane<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Hierro" title="Fernando Hierro">Fernando Hierro</a> for McManaman's case, McManaman said he never ever heard from or met Eriksson again. Zidane went on to state England had made a mistake, and described McManaman with a rare passion as one of the highest quality players he ever played with: "I was surprised when McManaman was left out of the last England squad. I couldn't believe they would ignore a player of his quality. Now people are talking about the fact that maybe he will get his chance because David Beckham is injured. But McManaman is far better than just being a replacement for Beckham. McManaman should be in the starting line-up anyway."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup> Support for McManaman also came before the 2002 World Cup in the British media, after <a href="/wiki/Sky_Sports" title="Sky Sports">Sky Sports</a> published an article based on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/OPTA" title="OPTA">OPTA</a> statistics, revealing that despite a poor goalscoring record, McManaman had in fact an 88% dribbling completion rate (having embarked on a run every 17 minutes), and an 84% pass completion rate, all three of which were higher by over 15% than any English midfield Premiership player at the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup></p>
<p>However, by late 2001, after coming on as a substitute when England beat <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">Germany</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Germany_1%E2%80%935_England_(2001)" title="Germany 1â5 England (2001)">5â1</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Olympiastadion_(Munich)" title="Olympiastadion (Munich)">Olympiastadion</a>, McManaman put in an inept<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (October 2016)">according to whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> display against <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> that saw him banished from Eriksson's team,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> as that was his final game; making just one substitute appearance after that in the critical qualifier against Greece in 2001. Later that year, he did himself no favours by "choosing not to play" in the game against Sweden by calling the FA to have himself dropped from the squad,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> before assistant coach at the time, <a href="/wiki/Tord_Grip" title="Tord Grip">Tord Grip</a> "put the knife" in his international career when he said "McManaman has never played well for England"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> and following that, McManaman was not selected for another England squad.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Critics.27_and_fans.27_analysis">Critics' and fans' analysis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steve_McManaman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Critics' and fans' analysis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>McManaman was once described as "England's forgotten man"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup> but was also accused of being apathetic and having a laidback attitude and having a reputation for being a troublemaker, which began after an infamous "dentists' chair" incident before Euro '96,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> where along with <a href="/wiki/Teddy_Sheringham" title="Teddy Sheringham">Teddy Sheringham</a> and Gascoigne, McManaman was photographed drinking and accused of causing thousands of pounds worth of damage to a <a href="/wiki/Cathay_Pacific" title="Cathay Pacific">Cathay Pacific</a> first class <a href="/wiki/Flight" title="Flight">flight</a> <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_cabin" title="Aircraft cabin">cabin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> McManaman's reputation was also not aided by the fact that he was also known for being a serial <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prank" title="Prank">prankster</a> with Fowler,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> which did nothing to help new coaches' negative opinions about him,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup> with the Spice Boys' image also making it worse, although, colleague <a href="/wiki/Gareth_Southgate" title="Gareth Southgate">Gareth Southgate</a> did say McManaman and Fowler's antics though "silly", helped foster <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Team_spirit" title="Team spirit">team spirit</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> In 2004, certain journalists even called for McManaman to be included in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euro_2004" title="Euro 2004">Euro 2004</a> squad, arguing that McManaman's experience would have been worth his inclusion in the side alone,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-search.japantimes.co.jp_153-1"><a href="#cite_note-search.japantimes.co.jp-153">[153]</a></sup> but to no avail as McManaman himself decided to retire shortly after.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Style_of_play">Style of play</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steve_McManaman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Style of play">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>A hard-working, versatile and technically gifted player, McManaman was usually deployed as a <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Winger" title="Midfielder">winger</a>, or occasionally as a <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Central_midfielder" title="Midfielder">central</a> <a href="/wiki/Midfielder" title="Midfielder">midfielder</a>; his preferred position, however, was that of a more offensive and creative <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Attacking_midfielder" title="Midfielder">attacking midfielder</a>, an uncommon position in the Premier League throughout his career. McManaman was a quick, strong, creative, and energetic player, with good <a href="/wiki/Dribbling#Association_football" title="Dribbling">dribbling</a> ability, as well as accurate passing and <a href="/wiki/Cross_(football)" title="Cross (football)">crossing</a> ability with either foot, which allowed him to create chances and provide assists for team-mates as a <a href="/wiki/Playmaker" title="Playmaker">playmaker</a>. He was often criticised, however, for his inability to score many goals, although he would later improve upon this element of his game during his career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Post_playing_career">Post playing career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steve_McManaman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Post playing career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>McManaman retired from his playing career after being released by <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a> in 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> In early 2006, McManaman nearly came out of retirement to sign for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Rangers" title="Hong Kong Rangers">Hong Kong Rangers</a>, a club owned by an admirer of his football, <a href="/wiki/Carson_Yeung" title="Carson Yeung">Carson Yeung</a>, but the deal fell through due to McManaman's recurrent injuries which scuppered his fitness test.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film_and_charity_appearances.3B_UEFA_Ambassador">Film and charity appearances; UEFA Ambassador</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steve_McManaman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Film and charity appearances; UEFA Ambassador">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In October 2006, McManaman played in a charity match for Liverpool Legends against Celtic Legends.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup></p>
<p>In late 2006, McManaman joined production for the film, <i><a href="/wiki/Goal_II:_Living_the_Dream" title="Goal II: Living the Dream">Goal II: Living the Dream</a></i>, the sequel to <i><a href="/wiki/Goal!_(film)" title="Goal! (film)">Goal!</a></i>. By the time of release in 2007, McManaman had also become an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Associate_Producer" title="Associate Producer">Associate Producer</a> of the film,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup> and appears in the film as one of the coaching staff for <a href="/wiki/Kuno_Becker" title="Kuno Becker">Kuno Becker</a>'s lead character. McManaman was also active in promoting the film with star <a href="/wiki/Anna_Friel" title="Anna Friel">Anna Friel</a> at its premiere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup></p>
<p>In June 2008, McManaman participated in <a href="/wiki/Steve_Nash" title="Steve Nash">Steve Nash</a> and <a href="/wiki/Claudio_Reyna" title="Claudio Reyna">Claudio Reyna</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Showdown_in_Chinatown" title="Showdown in Chinatown">Showdown in Chinatown</a>, an 8-on-8 charity soccer game at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sara_D._Roosevelt_Park" title="Sara D. Roosevelt Park">Sara D. Roosevelt Park</a>. Nash scored two goals in his team's 8â5 victory, which included McManaman scoring one goal and making five of the goals in a team including <a href="/wiki/Thierry_Henry" title="Thierry Henry">Thierry Henry</a>, Robbie Fowler, <a href="/wiki/Jason_Kidd" title="Jason Kidd">Jason Kidd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baron_Davis" title="Baron Davis">Baron Davis</a>, and Suns teammates <a href="/wiki/Raja_Bell" title="Raja Bell">Raja Bell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leandro_Barbosa" title="Leandro Barbosa">Leandro Barbosa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2010, McManaman became an ambassador for <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a> alongside <a href="/wiki/Christian_Karembeu" title="Christian Karembeu">Christian Karembeu</a> in its Champions League Trophy World Tour, as well as at the Madrid Festival leading up to the Champions League 2010 Final at the Bernabeu.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup> McManaman, has also been taking part in several "legends" squads for testimonial matches and fundraisers, most notably, at domestic level with the likes of ex-Liverpool players, but also for the EFPA- European Association of Former Players- along with a host of retired stars like <a href="/wiki/Hristo_Stoichkov" title="Hristo Stoichkov">Hristo Stoichkov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Enzo_Scifo" title="Enzo Scifo">Enzo Scifo</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lothar_Matthaus" title="Lothar Matthaus">Lothar Matthaus</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup> In May 2010, McManaman played for the Real Madrid Veteranos against Milan AC's Glorie team for <a href="/wiki/Charitable_organization" title="Charitable organization">charity</a> known as the Corazon Classic- in front of a crowd of 80,000 at the Bernabeu, and in an all star game featuring <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emilio_Butragueno" title="Emilio Butragueno">Emilio Butragueno</a>, Figo, Zidane, <a href="/wiki/Chendo" title="Chendo">Chendo</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alfonso" title="Alfonso">Alfonso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paolo_Maldini" title="Paolo Maldini">Paolo Maldini</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cafu" title="Cafu">Cafu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rui_Costa" title="Rui Costa">Rui Costa</a> and other world class football stars to a great reception.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2011, McManaman joined a number of former star players including <a href="/wiki/Diego_Maradona" title="Diego Maradona">Diego Maradona</a> and former team-mates Luis Figo and Robbie Fowler in a select World XI to play against <a href="/wiki/Chechnya" title="Chechnya">Chechen</a> President <a href="/wiki/Ramzan_Kadyrov" title="Ramzan Kadyrov">Ramzan Kadyrov</a> and his select XI in a match to mark the opening of the new national stadium in the <a href="/wiki/Second_Chechen_War" title="Second Chechen War">war torn nation's</a> capital of <a href="/wiki/Grozny" title="Grozny">Grozny</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> The match drew criticism from some commentators and human rights groups due to Kadyrov's alleged <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a> abuses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> McManaman commented "This is not a piece of propaganda for usÂ ... We are not here politically. We are just here to play football."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup> In December 2011, McManaman was also invited to be a part of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">United Nations Development Programme</a> Football Squad by ex-team mates Zidane and Ronaldo (ambassadors of the UNDP), to take part in a series of friendly matches to raise funds known as <a href="/wiki/Match_Against_Poverty" title="Match Against Poverty">Match Against Poverty</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2012, McManaman was officially declared as UEFA's sole ambassador for the <a href="/wiki/2013_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2013 UEFA Champions League Final">2013 UEFA Champions League Final</a> to be held at Wembley.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uefa_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-uefa-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_work">Corporate work</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steve_McManaman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Corporate work">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In July 2007, McManaman was named <a href="/wiki/Executive_director" title="Executive director">executive director</a> of <a href="/wiki/Carson_Yeung" title="Carson Yeung">Carson Yeung</a>'s Hong Kong-<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Listed_company" title="Listed company">listed company</a> Grandtop International Holdings Ltd, which subsequently took a 29.9% stake in <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> side <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Birmingham_City" title="Birmingham City">Birmingham City</a>. In August 2009, Carson Yeung confirmed that once his proposed take-over of Birmingham City went through, a role at St. Andrews would be given to McManaman, although he did not specify what role that would be.,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup> and by 2010, McManaman was appointed as a board director at Birmingham City, where McManaman assured <a href="/wiki/Steve_Bruce" title="Steve Bruce">Steve Bruce</a> at the time that he was not part of some scheme to take over his job as coach.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup> On 4 June 2012 it was announced that he had resigned as an executive director of Birmingham International Holdings, the company that owns Birmingham City.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup> On 19 September 2012, the <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Stock_Exchange" title="Hong Kong Stock Exchange">Hong Kong Stock Exchange</a> criticised McManaman "...Â for failing to use best endeavours to procure Birmingham City International Holdings' compliance with the Exchange Listing Rules."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup> The exchange said the company failed to disclose a large deposit it had to make as it was preparing to buy the English football club Birmingham City in 2009. The exchange also said the purchase of the club should have been put to the company's shareholders for their approval, which it was not.</p>
<p>In 2007â08, McManaman also got involved with corporate dealings in Hong Kong with companies like Sure Trace Inc, which was set up by another <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Porn" title="Porn">porn</a> baron and <a href="/wiki/Stock_market" title="Stock market">stock market</a> and IT entrepreneur, James MacKay, who transferred 2/3 of the company to him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup> The company made news for wrong reasons as Sure Trace had made a number of major contract announcements which had not become actual, revenue-generating contracts and was delisted by the US <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Securities_and_Exchange_Commission" title="Securities and Exchange Commission">Securities and Exchange Commission</a> (SEC). The company then setup True Product ID as a company to conduct technology joint ventures in China and the company was transferred to McManaman. To protect investors, the SEC suspended Sure Trace Security in August 2005, citing the accuracy of public information regarding its technology sales.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Management_intentions_.26_Coaching_Role">Management intentions &amp; Coaching Role</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steve_McManaman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Management intentions &amp; Coaching Role">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In January 2009, McManaman gave a press interview where he revealed his intention to go into management. "I'm still thinking of getting back into the game and hopefully I will do my coaching badges at some point this yearÂ ... It is going to be hard, though. There seems to be far less jobs available for the younger guys. Paul Ince, Roy Keane, Tony Adams â it seems as if people have got it in for them. It's becoming a bit less attractiveÂ ... If I do get back in, I don't want to be a coachÂ ... I want to be a manager, but that's easier said than doneÂ ... I want to be able to pick the team, make the decisions and everything that goes with it. That said, I can't do anything without my badges", he told the <i><a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Echo" title="Liverpool Echo">Liverpool Echo</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2013 it was announced by <a href="/wiki/Brendan_Rodgers" title="Brendan Rodgers">Brendan Rodgers</a> that McManaman would be taking up a coaching role with Liverpool F.C. at the academy to help nurture the club's future talents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_career">Media career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steve_McManaman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Media career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>McManaman first got a taste for media work in 2005 after he became active as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freelance" title="Freelance">freelance</a> <a href="/wiki/Mass_media" title="Mass media">media</a> <a href="/wiki/Sports_commentator" title="Sports commentator">commentator</a> and pundit, providing analysis to <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_channel)" title="ITV (TV channel)">ITV</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2005_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2005 UEFA Champions League Final">2005 UEFA Champions League Final</a>, in which he provided the analysis as his old club Liverpool won the trophy. McManaman then went on to take up opportunities for Asia's largest football broadcasters, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ESPN_Star" title="ESPN Star">ESPN Star</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a> in 2006, where he worked alongside commentator <a href="/wiki/John_Dykes" title="John Dykes">John Dykes</a> and ex-players such as fellow ex-Liverpool star <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Steve_McMahon_(footballer)" title="Steve McMahon (footballer)">Steve McMahon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup></p>
<p>By 2007, also McManaman became a full-time media pundit, having joined <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Setanta_Sports" title="Setanta Sports">Setanta Sports</a> as a football <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Color_analyst" title="Color analyst">analyst</a> and, for the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_in_English_football" title="2007â08 in English football">2007â08</a> season, he was given his own television show -<i>Macca's Monday Night</i>- reflecting on life in the Barclays Premier League.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup> On the show, he played host and was joined by <a href="/wiki/Neil_Warnock" title="Neil Warnock">Neil Warnock</a>, the former <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_United_F.C." title="Sheffield United F.C.">Sheffield United</a> manager, James Richardson, <a href="/wiki/Emmanuel_Petit" title="Emmanuel Petit">Emmanuel Petit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tim_Sherwood" title="Tim Sherwood">Tim Sherwood</a> and <a href="/wiki/Les_Ferdinand" title="Les Ferdinand">Les Ferdinand</a>. The show was finally axed in favour of "Football Matters", a live late Monday-night discussion show hosted by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_Richardson_(television_presenter)" title="James Richardson (television presenter)">James Richardson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rebecca_Lowe" title="Rebecca Lowe">Rebecca Lowe</a>. Renowned for his direct comments, in one of McManaman's broadcasts in February 2008, McManaman found himself criticised in the Liverpool press and by former Liverpool fans when his comments for Setanta after a Merseyside derby, on the ownership issue concerning <a href="/wiki/Debt" title="Debt">debt</a> involving <a href="/wiki/Tom_Hicks" title="Tom Hicks">Tom Hicks</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_N._Gillett,_Jr." title="George N. Gillett, Jr.">George N. Gillett, Jr.</a> at Anfield went down poorly with the supporters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since July 2010, having joined commentator Ian Darke and former <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">Germany</a> coach <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCrgen_Klinsmann" title="JÃ¼rgen Klinsmann">JÃ¼rgen Klinsmann</a> as well as Dutch International <a href="/wiki/Ruud_Gullit" title="Ruud Gullit">Ruud Gullit</a> on the <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a> coverage team as a commentary analyst for the <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010 World Cup</a>, McManaman has since signed on with the network to be an in-game analyst for the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Soccer" title="Major League Soccer">Major League Soccer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a>, and even 2013 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Confederations_Cup" title="Confederations Cup">Confederations Cup</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup_2014" title="FIFA World Cup 2014">FIFA World Cup 2014</a>, and has become a permanent co-commentator alongside <a href="/wiki/Ian_Darke" title="Ian Darke">Ian Darke</a>. In late November 2010 and in May 2011, McManaman was the halftime in-studio analyst alongside Gary Lineker and <a href="/wiki/Trevor_Francis" title="Trevor Francis">Trevor Francis</a> for La Liga's <a href="/wiki/El_Cl%C3%A1sico" title="El ClÃ¡sico">El ClÃ¡sico</a> broadcast on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al_Jazeera_Sports_%2B3" title="Al Jazeera Sports +3">Al Jazeera Sports +3</a>. McManaman and Darke were the main ESPN commentary team for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euro_2012" title="Euro 2012">Euro 2012</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup> while McManaman was also a guest on daily panel show, ESPN <a href="/wiki/PressPass" title="PressPass">PressPass</a> (now re-branded as <a href="/wiki/ESPN_FC" title="ESPN FC">ESPN FC</a>), alongside <a href="/wiki/Steve_Nicol" title="Steve Nicol">Steve Nicol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robbie_Mustoe" title="Robbie Mustoe">Robbie Mustoe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shaka_Hislop" title="Shaka Hislop">Shaka Hislop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robbie_Earle" title="Robbie Earle">Robbie Earle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gabriele_Marcotti" title="Gabriele Marcotti">Gabriele Marcotti</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup></p>
<p>From the 2013â14 season, McManaman joined <a href="/wiki/BT_Sport" title="BT Sport">BT Sport</a> as one of its lead pundits for its new Premiership coverage,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup> and McManaman was known for his frank yet candid comments that despite tendentiously staying safe and stating the obvious, were always good humoured. He was also known for his flamboyant dress sense â once causing a <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> stir for turning up to a live broadcast in an <a href="/wiki/Inspector_Gadget_(franchise)" title="Inspector Gadget (franchise)">Inspector Gadget</a>-like outfit<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steve_McManaman&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Together with Robbie Fowler, McManaman has invested in several racehorses through a company named <i>The Macca and Growler Partnership</i>, their most prolific horse being Seebald, winner of 2003 <a href="/wiki/Celebration_Chase" title="Celebration Chase">Queen Elizabeth the Queen Mother Celebration Chase</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[234]</a></sup> In 2013, veteran <a href="/wiki/Jockey" title="Jockey">jockey</a> <a href="/wiki/Tony_McCoy" title="Tony McCoy">Tony McCoy</a> named his horse for the <a href="/wiki/Chepstow" title="Chepstow">Chepstow</a> races, "El Macca" in reference to McManaman<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup></p>
<p>McManaman's grandfather was a <a href="/wiki/Bookmaker" title="Bookmaker">bookmaker</a> and his father described the family as having "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Horseracing" title="Horseracing">horseracing</a> in their blood."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup> According to the English FA website, McManaman is a distant relative of <a href="/wiki/Callum_McManaman" title="Callum McManaman">Callum McManaman</a>, who currently plays professional football as a winger at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Bromwich_Albion" title="West Bromwich Albion">West Bromwich Albion</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237">[237]</a></sup></p>
<p>McManaman married his longtime girlfriend, Victoria Edwards, a <a href="/wiki/Barrister#England_and_Wales" title="Barrister">barrister</a> and law lecturer (who taught at the <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_University_of_Madrid" title="Autonomous University of Madrid">Autonomous University of Madrid</a> during her time in Madrid with McManaman), on 6 June 2002, in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mallorca" title="Mallorca">Mallorca</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Palma_Cathedral" title="Palma Cathedral">Palma Cathedral</a>. Victoria gave birth to their daughters Ella in 2006 and Lara in 2009, and son Lucas James in 2012. The family divides its time between homes in <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Palma" title="Bay of Palma">Bay of Palma</a>, London and <a href="/wiki/Cheshire" title="Cheshire">Cheshire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[238]</a></sup></p>
